<div id="review_2438798759" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2438798759" />
    <a title="Brierly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25485458-brierly"><img alt="Brierly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421634217p2/25485458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2438798759?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brierly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brierly" href="/user/show/25485458-brierly">Brierly</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/33876452-inside-out-back-again">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25485458-brierly?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2438798759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6562062372377626860"><i>Inside Out & Back Again</i> is the debut novel from Thanhha Lai, who incorporates her own childhood memories of fleeing the Vietnam war as a refugee to Alabama in the 1970s. I love middle grades quasi-memoir, especially when I see that it is written in verse, so I pinned this one to the top of my TBR when a student mentioned it to me earlier in 2019. This is the first book I have read while being absolutely positive that I will be teaching sixth grade English (!) for the foreseeable future. Reading </span>
  <span id="freeText6562062372377626860" style="display:none"><i>Inside Out &amp; Back Again</i> is the debut novel from Thanhha Lai, who incorporates her own childhood memories of fleeing the Vietnam war as a refugee to Alabama in the 1970s. I love middle grades quasi-memoir, especially when I see that it is written in verse, so I pinned this one to the top of my TBR when a student mentioned it to me earlier in 2019. This is the first book I have read while being absolutely positive that I will be teaching sixth grade English (!) for the foreseeable future. Reading <i>Inside Out</i> was the perfect appetizer to the piles and piles of middle grades books that I have stockpiled while oscillating between wanting to teach high school English (mostly YA) and middle school English (mostly middle grades).<br /><br />Hà is ten years old in 1975. The story begins on Tết, where Hà and her entire family mark the calendar one year older. Hà lives in Saigon and if you needed a quick refresher on the Vietnam war (I did!) her family is politically aligned with South Vietnam, and therefore, aligned with the United States and capitalist democracy. Hà, her mother, and her three brothers are anxious about the fate of their father, who is a P.O.W. in North Vietnam. The novel does an excellent job of contrasting the visceral fear of living in a war zone with the cultural touchstones that make Saigon home to Hà, like eating juicy papaya and the mouth-watering umami saltiness of nước mắm (a.k.a. fish sauce).<br /><br /><i>Our lives<br />will twist and twist,<br />intermingling the old and the new<br />until it doesn't matter<br />which is which.</i><br /><br />If you read the summary, you know that Hà will become a refugee bound for Alabama, so I am not too worried about spoilers in revealing that. I was drawn to this narrative because of the setting during the fall of Saigon and Hà's subsequent relocation to Alabama, but it was the emotional details from Hà's coming-of-age experience that won me over. Perhaps it is the blend of Thanhha Lai's powerful memories with the creative liberty to reinterpret Hà as a fictional narrator. Recommended to those who love multi-hyphenate reading because this is certainly a middle-grades-historical-fiction-written-in-verse not to miss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6562062372377626860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2554839379" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2554839379" />
    <a title="Katherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine"><img alt="Katherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577842427p2/13311251.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2554839379?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/13311251-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/39963468-inside-out-back-again">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=everyone-loves-but-me">everyone-loves-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13311251-katherine?shelf=kick-ass-mc">kick-ass-mc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2554839379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13487537927428691286"><b>
  <i>”No one would believe me<br/>but at times <br/>I would chose <br/>wartime in Saigon<br/>over<br/>peacetime in Alabama."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Ten-year-old Hà lives in South Vietnam at a time of political turmoil in her country. Her father has been presumed missing in action for many years and her family is living on the brink of poverty in the aftermath of the Vietnam War. When the political unrest becomes too much for them, they flee by boat to America. There Hà, her three brothers and mother must get used to living in this strange land </span>
  <span id="freeText13487537927428691286" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”No one would believe me<br />but at times <br />I would chose <br />wartime in Saigon<br />over<br />peacetime in Alabama."</i>
</b><br /><br />Ten-year-old Hà lives in South Vietnam at a time of political turmoil in her country. Her father has been presumed missing in action for many years and her family is living on the brink of poverty in the aftermath of the Vietnam War. When the political unrest becomes too much for them, they flee by boat to America. There Hà, her three brothers and mother must get used to living in this strange land called America and make it their own. <br /><br />This was an exceedingly quick read that had a very impactful story. Hà had a lot of pluck and spunk that made her an appealing character to read about. Hearing about her struggles to fit in and adjust to such a different life were both heartbreaking and hopeful to read about. She never lost her fierce optimism that things would get better and her refusal to give up.<br /><br />For some reason, though, I felt that there was a slight disconnect between me and the overall storyline. I can't put my finger on what it was, though, which makes things super frustrating. This was not a bad book at all by any means. However, I felt like it was missing something that I can't quite describe. Maybe it's because this book takes place over the period of just one year and I felt like I wanted more out of Hà's story and her development?<br /><br />Despite feeling a slight disconnect between the overall storyline, this is a very impactful story I definitely think kids should read. The subject is as relevant now as it was when the events were happening, and it can teach them about accepting others and being inclusive to all.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Zoe&#39;s Human" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17061542-zoe-s-human"><img alt="Zoe&#39;s Human" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526828338p2/17061542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2198134192?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe&#39;s Human" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe&#39;s Human" href="/user/show/17061542-zoe-s-human">Zoe&#39;s Human</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061962790" href="/book/show/15818146-inside-out-and-back-again">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17061542-zoe-s-human?shelf=lt">lt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2198134192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10210582342220422833">No matter how old you are, whether or not you like poetry or not, you should still read this. I'm 45, I'm not into poetry, and I loved this. In spare but elegant verse, the story of one year in the life of a girl is told. A year where Saigon falls and her family becomes refugees fleeing to safety in the United States. A year of coming to terms with a new culture and language. A year of struggle as a forced immigrant. This is amazing both as a piece of literature and as a learning experience.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2175980589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2175980589" />
    <a title="Tamanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72441389-tamanna"><img alt="Tamanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535650820p2/72441389.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_3405263287" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3405263287" />
    <a title="Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72793544-tichana-the-book-hobbit"><img alt="Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598682051p2/72793544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3405263287?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) " href="/user/show/72793544-tichana-the-book-hobbit">Tichana  (The Book Hobbit) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72793544-tichana-the-book-hobbit?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72793544-tichana-the-book-hobbit?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3405263287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15346750775231176387"><i> They’re heading to Vūng Táu<br/>he says,<br/>where the rich go<br/>to flee Vietnam<br/>on cruise ships.<br/>I’m glad we’ve become poor<br/>so we can stay. <br/> -Early March </i> <br/><br/><br/>I don't think I have one bad thing to say about this book. <br/>This book gave me life today. I loved everything about it! I think cause it reminded me so much of when I immigrated to Canada after fleeing Iraq. It felt like home. <br/><br/>In this wonderful book we follow the story of Hà. A vietnamese girl in 1975 who is struggling with her family to either stay or leave </span>
  <span id="freeText15346750775231176387" style="display:none"><i> They’re heading to Vūng Táu<br />he says,<br />where the rich go<br />to flee Vietnam<br />on cruise ships.<br />I’m glad we’ve become poor<br />so we can stay. <br /> -Early March </i> <br /><br /><br />I don't think I have one bad thing to say about this book. <br />This book gave me life today. I loved everything about it! I think cause it reminded me so much of when I immigrated to Canada after fleeing Iraq. It felt like home. <br /><br />In this wonderful book we follow the story of Hà. A vietnamese girl in 1975 who is struggling with her family to either stay or leave South Vietnam after the Communism party is taking over. Part 2 and 3 of the book deals with the sea and residing in Alabama eventually. <br /><br />I loved the writing style and how beautiful were the emotions displayed by Hà. I was saddened by the racism, by the fear of the unknown and what refugee life feels like and how much it hurts. <br /><br />This book taught me new things about Vietnam. Of Papaya trees and rice cakes. Of Saigon and its beautiful people. It gave me perspective. <br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who wants to follow the journey of an immigrant family who hopes to end wars, of better life, of home sickness, and of racism and its effects on humanity. It's a beautiful book that brought laughter and tears to my eyes. Of a story I experienced and many other immigrants/refugees around the world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15346750775231176387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2792734800?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tasha " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tasha " href="/user/show/3589603-tasha">Tasha </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3589603-tasha?shelf=poetry-free-verse">poetry-free-verse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3589603-tasha?shelf=mg-and-ya">mg-and-ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2792734800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11540563381086742133">I'm sold! If you asked me as early as last week "do you read poetry?" I'd answer with a resounding "no, absolutely not!". Fast forward to today and I would say "is it free verse? Then absolutely yes!". I've never heard of free verse poetry but I like it! <br/><br/>Inside Out & Back Again is a year's journey told through verse of a young immigrant girl fleeing from Saigon. I felt like I got to know her through the sparse and beautiful poetry/verse. This book has been on the NYTimes Bestseller list, a Newbe</span>
  <span id="freeText11540563381086742133" style="display:none">I'm sold! If you asked me as early as last week "do you read poetry?" I'd answer with a resounding "no, absolutely not!". Fast forward to today and I would say "is it free verse? Then absolutely yes!". I've never heard of free verse poetry but I like it! <br /><br />Inside Out &amp; Back Again is a year's journey told through verse of a young immigrant girl fleeing from Saigon. I felt like I got to know her through the sparse and beautiful poetry/verse. This book has been on the NYTimes Bestseller list, a Newberry Honor Books and a National Book Award Winner and I'm sure several other prize lists for good reason. I'm looking forward to reading more from this genre.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dMvhH9ygnhNGgNNAo/RnCC53fSPSp/RXusrPOdULxLujnK3lHrw+JOgsq3M7A/4tXu1RLbwbZP1JmKriP8TI0A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8nIAjFbplNQMTTBTTP+CN8fO0zmKvrouo+E2sFTmsRwlJUx2lPU046LhSGDUCBsSt1T/N+QCKoRQs1Nrvim9dw==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4106652.Thanhha_Lai">About Thanhha Lai</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4106652.Thanhha_Lai"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1576616742p3/4106652.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4106652.Thanhha_Lai">Thanhha Lai
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
487
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6189341881389320330">Thanhha Lai was born in Vietnam. At the end of the war, she fled with her family to Alabama. There, she learned English from fourth graders and then spent the next decade correcting her grammar. Starting her writing life as a journalist, she worked at The Orange County Register. She switched to fiction, leading to an MFA from New York University and short story publications in various journals and</span>
  <span id="freeText6189341881389320330" style="display:none">Thanhha Lai was born in Vietnam. At the end of the war, she fled with her family to Alabama. There, she learned English from fourth graders and then spent the next decade correcting her grammar. Starting her writing life as a journalist, she worked at The Orange County Register. She switched to fiction, leading to an MFA from New York University and short story publications in various journals and anthologies. Then came <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8537327-inside-out-back-again" rel="nofollow noopener">"Inside Out &amp; Back Again"</a>, a National Book Award and Newbery Honor-winning verse novel based in part on her childhood as a refugee in Alabama. Next was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22477286-listen-slowly" rel="nofollow noopener">"Listen, Slowly"</a>, another middle grade novel featuring a young Vietnamese-American girl. Her most recent work, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41453635-butterfly-yellow" rel="nofollow noopener">"Butterfly Yellow"</a>, is also her first foray into the YA genre. Lai lives with her husband, daughter and a little white dog in New York City.<br /><br />To stay updated about Thanhha's writing, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thanhhalai.com">www.thanhhalai.com</a> and follow her on social media:<br /><br /><b>Facebook:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://facebook.com/ThanhhaLaiWriter">facebook.com/ThanhhaLaiWriter</a><br /><br /><b>Twitter:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twitter.com/ThanhhaLai">twitter.com/ThanhhaLai</a><br /><br /><b>Instagram:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://instagram.com/thanhha_lai">instagram.com/thanhha_lai</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6189341881389320330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
